Linguistic Analysis of the Word Mu'jiz
Explains the etymology and morphology of the word mu'jiz.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic derivation and morphological significance of the word 'mu'jiz' (miracle) in Islamic theology.

Core Idea
The term 'mu'jiz' emphasizes the incapacity of others through its linguistic form.

Before we can fully grasp the theological concept of miracles in Islam, we must first understand the word itself. This passage from Imam Nasafi's *Tabsirat al-Adilla* examines the etymology and morphology of 'mu'jiz'. It shows how the word is derived from 'ajz' (incapacity) and uses a feminine suffix for exaggeration, similar to other Arabic words.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Notice the author's concise style.
Pay attention to the comparison between mu'jiz and muqaddir.
2
Identify the derivation pattern
Notice that 'mu'jiz' follows the same pattern as 'muqaddir'. Both are based on root meanings related to capacity or incapacity.
This shows how kalam uses linguistic patterns.
3
Understand the hā' suffix
The feminine hā' in 'mu'jiza' is not for gender but for exaggeration. Think of examples like 'ʿallāma' (very learned).
This is a key point: morphology can convey meaning beyond grammar.
4
Reflect on theological significance
Consider why the term emphasizes the incapacity of the people. This sets up the concept of miracle as a proof of prophethood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم المعجز في الحقيقة وإن كان اسماً لمثبت العجز كالمقدر اسم لمثبت القدرة إلا أن المظهر للعجز يسمى به مجازا، ثم الهاء الداخلة في لفظها للمبالغة، كما في العلامة والنسابة والراوية، فكانت داخلة فيها للمبالغة في الخبر عن عجز المرسل إليهم.
Then the miracle (al-mu'jiz) in reality, although it is a noun for that which establishes incapacity, just as 'the one who measures' (al-muqaddir) is a noun for that which establishes ability, except that the one who manifests incapacity is called by it metaphorically. Then the feminine 'hā' that enters into its word is for exaggeration, as in 'the very knowledgeable' (al-ʿallāma), 'the genealogist' (al-nassāba), and 'the narrator' (al-rāwiya). Thus it entered into it for exaggeration in the report about the incapacity of those sent to.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage provides a linguistic analysis of the term 'mu'jiz' (miracle). It first explains that, like 'muqaddir' (one who measures/predestines) is derived from 'qudra' (power), 'mu'jiz' is derived from 'ʿajz' (incapacity). However, the one who manifests the incapacity of others is called 'mu'jiz' metaphorically. The author then notes that the feminine 'hā' suffix in the word (as in 'mu'jiza') is for exaggeration (mubālagha), similar to words like 'ʿallāma' (very learned) and 'nassāba' (expert genealogist). Thus the term emphasizes the extreme incapacity of the people the prophet is sent to in the face of the miracle.

Key Terms
معجز (mu'jiz)
مقدر (muqaddir)
عجز (ʿajz)
قدرة (qudra)
مبالغة (mubālagha)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The feminine suffix in 'mu'jiza' indicates femininity of the miracle.
Correction: The suffix indicates exaggeration, as the author explains by citing analogous words like 'ʿallāma'.

Checkpoint
What is the function of the feminine hā' in the word mu'jiza according to this passage?
A) To indicate the feminine gender of the miracle
B) To signify exaggeration in causing incapacity
C) To show that the miracle is a verbal noun
D) To denote the recipient of the miracle

Key Takeaway
The term 'mu'jiz' linguistically emphasizes the incapacity of others through its derivation from 'ajz' and the use of the feminine hā' for exaggeration.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear the word 'mu'jiza' (miracle), do you think of it as evidence of your own weakness or as proof of the prophet's strength? Based on this lesson, which view does the Arabic language demand you adopt? How will that shift your mindset when you next hear a miracle story?
?
The feminine 'ha' in 'mu'jiza' is not for femininity but to exaggerate the incapacity of the people. Have you ever felt utterly incapable in front of something you knew was from Allah? How did that feeling draw you closer to faith or test your patience? Commit to remembering this linguistic nuance the next time you feel overwhelmed.
?
This lesson shows that the primary meaning of 'mu'jiz' is the miracle itself, not the prophet. Are you someone who tends to focus on the personalities (the messengers) rather than the signs (the miracles)? How can you train your heart to look at the signs as direct proofs from Allah, not just as stories of men?

Capability: Two Dimensions of Power in Kalam
Definition and bipartite division of capability (istita'a).

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the kalam distinction between capability as preparatory conditions (soundness of causes) and capability as the accident enabling voluntary action.

Core Idea
Capability in kalam is not one thing; it has a before and a during.

Theologians use several words—istita'a, qudra, quwwa, taqa—almost interchangeably, but when analyzing the reality behind them, they recognize two distinct aspects. Imam Nasafi's passage from Tabsirat al-Adilla lays out this crucial division: one part concerns the soundness of instruments that precedes the action, the other concerns the very power that attends the act itself. Let's examine his precise definitions.

Guided Path
1
Encounter the synonyms
Read the Arabic and translation noting that istita'a, qudra, quwwa, and taqa are used as near‑synonyms in kalam terminology.
This removes confusion about different terms—they all refer to the same concept when applied to servants.
2
Find the two divisions
After the synonyms, the author states that 'power and capability' are of two divisions. Identify each one in the text.
The first division is described as 'soundness of causes and health of instruments' and can precede the action.
3
Understand the first type
The first type is defined as 'preparedness for executing the action upon the will of the chooser.' It is not an actual cause but a blessing from Allah.
This type includes things like having working limbs and tools.
4
Grasp the second type
The second type is a 'meaning' (an accident) that Allah creates in the living being, by which it performs voluntary actions. It is a real cause and exists only for the action.
This accident does not precede the action; it is simultaneous with it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
٣- الكلام في الاستطاعة: اعلم أن الاستطاعة والقوة والقدرة والطاقة متقاربة المعاني، وفي مصطلح أهل الكلام أنهم يريدون بها كلها شيئا واحدًا إذا أضافوها إلى العباد ويجعلونها في عرفهم بمنزلة الأسماء المترادفة كالأسد والليث وأشباه ذلك. [أقسام الاستطاعة]: ثم الأصل أن المسمى باسم القدرة والاستطاعة عندنا قسمان: أحدهما سلامة الأسباب وصحة الآلات وهي قد تتقدم الأفعال، وحقيقتها ليست بمحصولة عللاً للأفعال وإن كانت الأفعال لا تقوم إلا بها لكنها نعم من الله تعالى يكرم بها من يشاء ثم يستأديهم شكرها عند احتمالهم العلم بالنعم وبلوغ عقولهم الوقوف عليها، وهذا النوع من الاستطاعة يحد بأنها: التهيؤ لتنفيذ الفعل عند إرادة المختار. والقسم الثاني: معنى لا يمكن تبين حده بمعنى يشار إليه سوى أنه ليس إلا للفعل، وهو عرض يخلقه الله تعالى في الحيوان يفعل به أفعاله الاختيارية وهو علة
3. Discussion on capability (istiṭāʿa): Know that capability, strength (quwwa), power (qudra), and capacity (ṭāqa) are close in meaning. And in the terminology of the theologians (ahl al-kalām), they intend by all of them one thing when they attribute them to servants, and they consider them, in their convention, as synonymous names, like 'asad' and 'layth' and the like. [Divisions of capability]: Then the principle is that what is named by the name 'power' and 'capability' with us is of two divisions: One of them is the soundness of causes (salāmat al-asbāb) and the health of instruments (ṣiḥḥat al-ālāt), and it may precede actions. Its reality is not actual as causes for actions, even though actions are only established through them, but they are blessings from Allah the Exalted with which He honors whomever He wills, then He demands of them their gratitude when they are capable of knowledge of blessings and their minds reach understanding them. This type of capability is defined as: preparedness (tahayyuʾ) for executing the action upon the will of the chooser. And the second division: a meaning (maʿnā) whose definition cannot be clarified by a meaning to which one points, except that it is only for the action. It is an accident (ʿaraḍ) that Allah the Exalted creates in the animal, by which he performs his voluntary actions, and it is a cause (ʿilla).
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification of capability (istiṭāʿa) as understood in kalām. The author begins by stating that terms like istiṭāʿa, quwwa, qudra, and ṭāqa are near-synonyms; in kalām terminology, when attributed to servants, they refer to the same concept, much like 'asad' and 'layth' both mean lion. Then, under the subheading 'Divisions of capability', the author explains that what is called power and capability is of two types. The first type is 'soundness of causes and health of instruments'—these can precede the action and are not actual causes of actions in themselves, but actions depend on them. They are blessings from God, for which He may demand gratitude. This type is defined as 'preparedness for executing the action upon the will of the chooser.' The second type is a 'meaning' (maʿnā) that cannot be defined by pointing to another meaning; it exists only for the action. It is an accident created by God in the living being, by which the being performs voluntary actions, and it is a cause. The passage ends mid-sentence on the page, likely continuing to describe this second type further.

Key Terms
استطاعة
قدرة
قوة
طاقة
تهيؤ
عرض
علة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Capability is a single, uniform concept.
Correction: Kalam distinguishes between preparatory conditions (which can precede action) and the co-occurring power (which is only for the action).

Checkpoint
How many divisions of capability (istiṭāʿa) does the author mention in this passage?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) Four

Key Takeaway
Capability in kalam consists of two distinct aspects: preparatory conditions (soundness of instruments) that precede the action, and the co-occurring accident of power that is the direct cause of voluntary action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever blamed your lack of 'sound health' for not doing good, forgetting that even the preparedness is a blessing from Allah for which He demands gratitude? How will you thank Him for the limbs and tools He has given you before action?
?
If the actual power to act is created only at the moment of action by Allah, what does that mean for your pride in your achievements? Can you truly claim any ability as your own, or are you entirely dependent on His moment-by-moment creation?
?
Consider a sin you fell into despite being physically prepared. What does this lesson teach you about where the real power to choose right lies? Will you now ask Allah for both the preparatory health and the co-occurring power before every action?

Two Types of Capacity in the Quran
Nasafi distinguishes two types of capacity using Quranic proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Quranic distinction between capacity of means (istita'at al-asbab) and true capacity (haqiqat al-qudra), and why only the absence of true capacity incurs blame.

Core Idea
Not all 'istita'a' in the Quran refers to the same power; one is physical means, the other is moral capacity.

The Quran uses the word 'istita'a' in different contexts to refer to two distinct realities: the external means (like provision and health) and the internal true capacity that makes an act morally chargeable. Imam al-Nasafi clarifies this distinction by examining verses that mention blame and verses that mention means, helping us understand the basis of moral responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that the author repeats 'yuhaqqiqu' (he verifies) to emphasize his reasoning.
2
Identify the two types of capacity
The passage presents evidence for two types: capacity of means (e.g., provision and mount for Hajj) and true capacity (e.g., ability to hear). Find the Quranic verses for each.
The verse about 'not having the means' (4:25) is for capacity of means; 'they were not able to hear' (11:20) is for true capacity.
3
Understand the blame distinction
The author argues that blame only attaches to absence of true capacity when means are present. The absence of means is not blameworthy because it is not under one's control.
Consider the story of Moses and Khidr: Moses lacked true patience, not the means (he was physically capable).
4
Reflect on the moral implication
Ask yourself: How does this distinction help resolve apparent contradictions in Quranic verses about human capacity?
This connects to the broader kalam debate on human free will and divine justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحققه أن أهل النفاق كانوا عوام، وقدرة العمل التي توجب حصول الفعل ويتكلم فيها المتكلمون أنها مع الفعل أو قبله وتبقى أو لا تبقى مما لا يعرفه العوام ولا يصورونها في الأوهام، وذلك قوله تعالى: وَمَن لَّمْ يَسْتَطِعْ مِنكُمْ طَوْلًا والمراد به استطاعة الآلات، وكذا قوله تعالى: وَلِلَّهِ عَلَى النَّاسِ حِجُّ الْبَيْتِ مَنِ اسْتَطَاعَ إِلَيْهِ سَبِيلًا والمراد به الزاد والراحلة لا حقيقة قدرة الفعل، فهذه الآيات دليل ثبوت استطاعة الأسباب والآلات. هناك استطاعة بمعنى حقيقة القدرة: وأما دليل ثبوت الاستطاعة التي هي حقيقة القدرة فقوله تعالى: مَا كَانُوا يَسْتَطِيعُونَ السَّمْعَ والمراد منه نفي حقيقة القدرة لا نفي الأسباب والآلات؛ لأنها كانت ثابتة، وإنما المنتفى عنهم كان حقيقة القدرة التي بها يتعلق الفعل. يحققه أنه ذكر ذلك على وجه الذم لهم، والذم إنما يلحقهم بانعدام حقيقة القدرة عند وجود الأسباب وصحة الآلات لا بانعدام سلامة الأسباب وصحة الآلات، لان انتفاء تلك الاستطاعة لم تكن بتضييعه بل هو في ذلك مجبور، وأما انتفاء حقيقة القدرة فموجب ذمهم؛ لأن انعدامها مع سلامة الأسباب وصحة الآلات كانت بتضييعه إياها لاشتغاله بضد ما أمر به. يحققه أنه خص بنفس هذه الاستطاعة الكافر، وانتفاء تلك الاستطاعة يستوي فيه المسلم والكافر، وإنما المختص بالكافر هو انتفاء هذه الاستطاعة، والدليل عليه قول صاحب موسى لموسى عليهما السلام: إِنَّكَ لَن تَسْتَطِيعَ مَعِيَ صَبْرًا وقوله: أَلَمْ أَقُلْ إِنَّكَ لَن تَسْتَطِيعَ مَعِيَ صَبْرًا والمراد منه حقيقة قدرة الصبر لا أسباب الصبر والآلة فإن تلك كانت ثابتة له. ألا ترى أنه عاتبه على ذلك ولا يلام من عدم آلات الفعل وأسبابه وإنما يلام من امتنع منه الفعل لتضييعه قدرة الفعل لاشتغاله بغير ما أمر به، وشغله إياها بضد ما أمر به والله الموفق.
He verifies that the people of hypocrisy were commoners, and the capacity for action which necessitates the occurrence of the act and about which the mutakallimun speak—whether it is with the act or before it, and whether it remains or does not remain—is something the common people do not know and cannot imagine. That is His saying: 'And whoever among you does not have the means'—and what is meant by it is the capacity of instruments. Likewise His saying: 'And for Allah is the pilgrimage to the House for whoever is able to find a way'—and what is meant by it is provision and mount, not the true capacity for the act. So these verses are evidence for the existence of capacity of causes and instruments. There is a capacity in the sense of true capacity: As for the evidence for the existence of capacity which is true capacity, it is His saying: 'They were not able to hear'—and what is meant by it is the negation of true capacity, not the negation of causes and instruments, because they were present. Rather, what was negated from them was true capacity by which the act is attached. He verifies that He mentioned this by way of blame for them. Blame only attaches to them due to the absence of true capacity when causes are present and instruments are sound, not due to the absence of soundness of causes and soundness of instruments, because the absence of that capacity was not due to their negligence, but rather they were compelled in that. As for the absence of true capacity, it necessitates blame for them, because its absence with soundness of causes and soundness of instruments was due to their negligence of it, due to their preoccupation with the opposite of what they were commanded. He verifies that this capacity is specifically [negated] for the disbeliever, while the absence of that [other] capacity is equal for the Muslim and the disbeliever. Rather, what is specific to the disbeliever is the absence of this capacity. The evidence for it is the saying of the companion of Moses to Moses, peace be upon them: 'Indeed, you will never be able to have patience with me,' and his saying: 'Did I not say that you will never be able to have patience with me?' And what is meant by it is the true capacity for patience, not the causes and instruments of patience, for those were present for him. Do you not see that he reproached him for that, and a person is not blamed for the absence of instruments and causes of an act, but rather he is blamed for refraining from the act due to his negligence of the capacity for the act due to his preoccupation with other than what he was commanded, and his using it for the opposite of what he was commanded. And Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 129

Commentary
This passage defines and proves two distinct types of istita'a (capacity/power). The author begins by noting that common people are unaware of the subtle debates among mutakallimun about whether capacity is simultaneous with or prior to the act, and whether it remains. He then presents Quranic evidence. First, he cites verses that refer to capacity of means and instruments (istita'at al-asbab wa al-alat), such as the verse about not having the means to marry free women (4:25) and the pilgrimage verse (3:97), interpreted as provision and mount. These establish one type of capacity. Second, he presents verses that refer to true capacity (haqiqat al-qudra), such as 'They were not able to hear' (11:20). This negation is of true capacity, not means, because the means (hearing faculties) were present. The fact that it is mentioned as blame indicates that blame attaches only to the absence of true capacity when means are sound. If means were absent, the person would be compelled and not blameworthy. The distinction is further illustrated by the story of Moses and Khidr: Moses was told he could not have patience, meaning true capacity for patience was negated, not the means (which were present). Moses was reproached because he lacked the true capacity due to his preoccupation. Thus, the author establishes that true capacity is what is subject to moral responsibility.

Key Terms
استطاعة
قدرة
استطاعة الأسباب
حقيقة القدرة
الذم
المتكلمون

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Thinking that all Quranic mentions of 'istita'a' refer to the same type of capacity.
Correction: The author shows that some verses refer to capacity of means (external instruments) while others refer to true capacity (internal moral power), and the consequences differ.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why is the disbeliever specifically blamed for the absence of true capacity, while the Muslim and disbeliever are equal in the absence of capacity of means?
A) Because capacity of means is not in one's control, so no blame attaches to its absence.
B) Because true capacity is the only capacity that leads to action.
C) Because disbelievers are compelled in all their actions.
D) Because the verse about hearing negates all capacity.

Key Takeaway
The Quran uses 'istita'a' in two distinct senses: capacity of means (which is not blameworthy if absent) and true capacity (whose absence incurs blame when means are present).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a setback in your religious duties, do you honestly examine whether the obstacle is within your control (lack of true capacity due to your own negligence) or do you attribute it to external circumstances? How can you take greater ownership of your spiritual capacity starting today?
?
Recall a situation where you had all the physical means to do good (e.g., health, wealth, knowledge) but you failed to act, blaming it on 'not being able'. In light of this lesson, what does that failure reveal about your true capacity? What practical step will you take to strengthen this inner capacity?
?
The people of hypocrisy are condemned not because they lacked physical ability, but because they misused their inner capacity. In your daily life, which distractions or preoccupations are draining your true capacity for obedience? What specific change will you commit to this week to redirect that capacity toward what pleases Allah?

The Denial of Human Capacity Refuted
Identifying the opponents and affirming istita'a as an accident.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Maturidi school affirms that human capacity (istita'a) is a real accident distinct from the person, and how this refutes the views of an-Nazzam and others who deny it.

Core Idea
Human capacity is a real accident, not just a description of the person.

The passage begins by identifying a group of theologians—an-Nazzam, 'Ali al-Uswari, and Abu Bakr al-Asamm—who claimed that there is no separate capacity; rather, a person is capable by his very self. The author firmly rejects this, asserting that capacity is an accident (arad) that exists beyond the essence. In this lesson, we examine this claim and the foundational assertion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the opponents and their view
Read the first sentence to see who the author is refuting and what they claim.
They say 'la istita'ata lil-insan' meaning no capacity exists as a separate entity.
2
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation to grasp the meaning.
Notice the structure: refutation then assertion.
3
Understand the key claim
The author asserts that istita'a is an accident beyond the essence, and reminds that an accident is a meaning beyond the body.
This is a foundational claim in Maturidi kalam.
4
Consider why the author insists on this
Think about the implications: if capacity were not an accident, then all actions would be directly from the essence, contradicting human responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبطل بهذا قول من يقول: لا استطاعة للإنسان إذ هي ليست معنى وراء المستطيع بل الإنسان مستطيع بنفسه لا باستطاعة كما ذهب إليه النظام وعلى الأسواري وأبو بكر الأصم. الاستطاعة عرض وراء الذات لأنا بينا بالدليل ثبوتها وهي عرض من الأعراض، ولا شك أن العرض معنى وراء الجسم، والذي يدل على ثبوتها أنا وجدنا الإنسان سليم الجوارح ليس بذي آفة وهو قادر على حمل خمسين رطلاً، ثم وجدناه في حالة أخرى قادرا على حمل مائة رطل من غير زيادة في أجزاء أعضائه، ونظيره خيطان منشوران يصعب قطعهما، وإذا فتلا يصعب القطع من غير زيادة في أجزاء الخيطين بل لحدوث الفتل وهو عرض في نفسه، وبهذا يبطل أيضًا قول غيلان وأتباعه.
And by this, the statement of those who say that there is no capacity for man is refuted, since it is not a meaning beyond the capable, but rather man is capable by himself without a capacity, as held by an-Nazzam, 'Ali al-Uswari, and Abu Bakr al-Asamm. Capacity is an accident beyond the essence. For we have demonstrated by evidence its existence, and it is an accident among accidents, and there is no doubt that an accident is a meaning beyond the body. What indicates its existence is that we find a person with sound limbs, not having a defect, capable of carrying fifty pounds, then we find him in another state capable of carrying one hundred pounds without any increase in the parts of his limbs. Its analogy is two untwisted threads whose cutting is difficult, and when they are twisted, the cutting becomes difficult without any increase in the parts of the two threads, but due to the occurrence of twisting, which is an accident in itself. And by this, the statement of Ghaylan and his followers is also refuted.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage refutes the denial of human capacity (istita'a) by proving it is an accident (arad) distinct from the body. The author first identifies the opponents: an-Nazzam, 'Ali al-Uswari, and Abu Bakr al-Asamm, who claimed that there is no separate capacity; rather, the person is capable by himself. The author asserts that capacity is an accident beyond the essence (dhāt), and that this has been demonstrated. The proof: a person with sound limbs can carry fifty pounds, and later carry one hundred pounds without any increase in his body parts. This variation must be due to an additional accident (capacity) that comes and goes. An analogy is given: two untwisted threads are already difficult to cut, but when twisted, cutting becomes even harder—not because of added matter, but because of the accident of twisting. Similarly, capacity is an accident that increases strength. This same proof also refutes Ghaylan and his followers, who likely held a similar denial or misunderstanding of capacity. Thus, the author establishes that human capacity is a real, non-essential attribute.

Correction: Capacity (istita'a) is a real accident that exists beyond the essence, as demonstrated by evidence.

Key Takeaway
The Maturidi school affirms that human capacity (istita'a) is a real accident that exists beyond the essence, contrary to the views of an-Nazzam and others.

Evidence for Istita'a as an Accident and Refutation of Ghaylan
Providing empirical and analogical evidence that istita'a is an accident.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two pieces of evidence—the weight-carrying example and the thread analogy—that prove human capacity is an accident, and how this refutes Ghaylan's view.

Core Idea
Variation in capability without bodily change proves capacity is an accident.

Having established that capacity is an accident, the author now provides concrete evidence. He gives two examples: a person who can carry different weights without any change in his limbs, and the analogy of threads that become harder to cut when twisted. These show that the increase in capability is due to an accident, not a change in the body's substance. The same proof also refutes Ghaylan and his followers.

Guided Path
1
Read the evidence passage
Read the Arabic and translation of the evidence section carefully.
This passage contains two analogies and a conclusion.
2
Examine the weight-carrying example
Notice how a person can carry 50 then 100 pounds without any increase in limb parts. This indicates an additional accident.
This is a direct empirical observation.
3
Analyze the thread analogy
Understand that twisting threads increases cutting difficulty without adding material, due to the accident of twisting.
This parallels the capacity increase.
4
Connect both to the definition of accident
Both examples show that a new attribute (accident) arises without change in the underlying substance.
This supports the claim that istita'a is an accident.
5
See how this refutes Ghaylan
The author states that the same proof refutes Ghaylan and his followers, who likely denied capacity as an accident.
This ties back to the overall refutation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبطل بهذا قول من يقول: لا استطاعة للإنسان إذ هي ليست معنى وراء المستطيع بل الإنسان مستطيع بنفسه لا باستطاعة كما ذهب إليه النظام وعلى الأسواري وأبو بكر الأصم. الاستطاعة عرض وراء الذات لأنا بينا بالدليل ثبوتها وهي عرض من الأعراض، ولا شك أن العرض معنى وراء الجسم، والذي يدل على ثبوتها أنا وجدنا الإنسان سليم الجوارح ليس بذي آفة وهو قادر على حمل خمسين رطلاً، ثم وجدناه في حالة أخرى قادرا على حمل مائة رطل من غير زيادة في أجزاء أعضائه، ونظيره خيطان منشوران يصعب قطعهما، وإذا فتلا يصعب القطع من غير زيادة في أجزاء الخيطين بل لحدوث الفتل وهو عرض في نفسه، وبهذا يبطل أيضًا قول غيلان وأتباعه.
And by this, the statement of those who say that there is no capacity for man is refuted, since it is not a meaning beyond the capable, but rather man is capable by himself without a capacity, as held by an-Nazzam, 'Ali al-Uswari, and Abu Bakr al-Asamm. Capacity is an accident beyond the essence. For we have demonstrated by evidence its existence, and it is an accident among accidents, and there is no doubt that an accident is a meaning beyond the body. What indicates its existence is that we find a person with sound limbs, not having a defect, capable of carrying fifty pounds, then we find him in another state capable of carrying one hundred pounds without any increase in the parts of his limbs. Its analogy is two untwisted threads whose cutting is difficult, and when they are twisted, the cutting becomes difficult without any increase in the parts of the two threads, but due to the occurrence of twisting, which is an accident in itself. And by this, the statement of Ghaylan and his followers is also refuted.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage refutes the denial of human capacity (istita'a) by proving it is an accident (arad) distinct from the body. The author first identifies the opponents: an-Nazzam, 'Ali al-Uswari, and Abu Bakr al-Asamm, who claimed that there is no separate capacity; rather, the person is capable by himself. The author asserts that capacity is an accident beyond the essence (dhāt), and that this has been demonstrated. The proof: a person with sound limbs can carry fifty pounds, and later carry one hundred pounds without any increase in his body parts. This variation must be due to an additional accident (capacity) that comes and goes. An analogy is given: two untwisted threads are already difficult to cut, but when twisted, cutting becomes even harder—not because of added matter, but because of the accident of twisting. Similarly, capacity is an accident that increases strength. This same proof also refutes Ghaylan and his followers, who likely held a similar denial or misunderstanding of capacity. Thus, the author establishes that human capacity is a real, non-essential attribute.

Proof that Capability is an Accident
Nasafi proves capability is an accident and refutes opposing views.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the proof that human capability (istiṭā‘a) is an accident (ʿaraḍ) distinct from the self, and how this refutes several opposing sectarian views.

Core Idea
Human capability is an additional accident, not the self or just sound limbs.

Imam Nasafi begins by invoking the Quranic story of Moses and Khidr to illustrate that capability is a real power, not merely the presence of instruments. He then provides a rational proof that capability is an accident distinct from the body, using examples of varying weight capacity and twisted threads. This proof serves to refute the claims of several theologians who denied capability as a separate entity.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the full Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the main argument and refutations.
Notice the use of Quranic verse at the beginning.
2
Identify the proof for capability as an accident
Find the observation of a person carrying different weights without bodily change and the analogy of twisted threads.
Both examples show increase in capability without increase in body parts.
3
Understand the refutations
Note how the proof refutes three opposing views: those denying capability, those reducing it to soundness, and those claiming it is part of the capable.
Each refutation is grounded in the proof that capability is an accident.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَلَمْ أَقُلْ إِنَّكَ لَن تَسْتَطِيعَ مَعِيَ صَبْرًا والمراد منه حقيقة قدرة الصبر لا أسباب الصبر والآلة فإن تلك كانت ثابتة له. ألا ترى أنه عاتبه على ذلك ولا يلام من عدم آلات الفعل وأسبابه وإنما يلام من امتنع منه الفعل لتضييعه قدرة الفعل لاشتغاله بغير ما أمر به، وشغله إياها بضد ما أمر به والله الموفق. وبطل بهذا قول من يقول: لا استطاعة للإنسان إذ هي ليست معنى وراء المستطيع بل الإنسان مستطيع بنفسه لا باستطاعة كما ذهب إليه النظام وعلى الأسواري وأبو بكر الأصم. لأنا بينا بالدليل ثبوتها وهي عرض من الأعراض، ولا شك أن العرض معنى وراء الجسم، والذي يدل على ثبوتها أنا وجدنا الإنسان سليم الجوارح ليس بذي آفة وهو قادر على حمل خمسين رطلاً، ثم وجدناه في حالة أخرى قادرا على حمل مائة رطل من غير زيادة في أجزاء أعضائه، ونظيره خيطان منشوران يصعب قطعهما، وإذا فتلا يصعب القطع من غير زيادة في أجزاء الخيطين بل لحدوث الفتل وهو عرض في نفسه، وبهذا يبطل أيضًا قول غيلان وأتباعه وثمامة بن الأشرس وبشر بن المعتمر: أن الاستطاعة ليست غير سلامة الأسباب وصحة الجوارح وتخليها عن الآفات. وبهذا أيضا يبطل قول ضرار وحفص الفرد أنها بعض المستطيع لما ثبت أنها عرض، والقول بكون العرض بعض الجسم محال. والله الموفق.
Did I not say that you will never be able to have patience with me? And what is intended by it is the reality of the power of patience, not the causes of patience and the instrument, for those were established for him. Do you not see that he reproached him for that, and one who lacks the instruments and causes of an act is not blamed, but rather one who refrains from the act due to his wasting the power of the act by occupying himself with other than what he was commanded, and occupying it with the opposite of what he was commanded, and God is the giver of success. And by this the statement of those who say, “There is no capability for the human,” is refuted, for it is not a meaning beyond the capable one, but rather the human is capable by himself without capability, as al-Nazzam, al-Uswari, and Abu Bakr al-Asamm held. For we have demonstrated by proof its existence, and it is an accident among accidents, and there is no doubt that the accident is a meaning beyond the body. And what indicates its existence is that we find a human with sound limbs, free from defect, capable of carrying fifty pounds; then we find him in another state capable of carrying a hundred pounds without an increase in the parts of his limbs. An analogy is two threads that are twisted, whose cutting becomes difficult, and when they are [ ? ] the cutting becomes difficult without an increase in the parts of the two threads, but due to the occurrence of twisting, which is an accident in itself. And by this also the statement of Ghilan and his followers, and Thumama ibn al-Ashras, and Bishr ibn al-Mu‘tamir is refuted: that capability is nothing but soundness of causes and health of limbs and their being free from defects. And by this also the statement of Dirar and Hafs al-Fard is refuted that it is a part of the capable one, because it has been established that it is an accident, and the statement that an accident is part of a body is impossible. And God is the giver of success.
Source pages p. 130

Commentary
This passage is a proof that human capability (istiṭā‘a) is an accident (ʿaraḍ) distinct from the self, combined with refutations of several opposing views. It begins with the Quranic verse 'Did I not say that you will never be able to have patience with me?' (Surah al-Kahf 75) and explains that what is meant by 'power of patience' is the reality of the power itself, not its causes or instruments, because those were already present for Moses (peace be upon him). The reproach indicates that blame attaches to wasting the power, not to lacking instruments. The author then states that this refutes the view of those who deny any capability for humans, such as al-Nazzam, al-Uswari, and Abu Bakr al-Asamm, who held that the human is capable by himself without any additional accident of capability. The proof that capability is an accident is given: we observe a sound-limbed person able to carry fifty pounds, then later the same person can carry a hundred pounds without any increase in his limbs; this increase cannot be attributed to the body itself, so it must be a supervening accident. An analogy is given of two threads: when separate they are easy to cut, but when twisted they become difficult to cut, not because the threads increased but because of the accident of twisting. This analogy refutes Ghilan, Thumama, and Bishr, who claimed capability is merely soundness of causes. Finally, Dirar and Hafs are refuted for claiming capability is part of the capable one, because an accident cannot be a part of a body.

D) It does not exist.

Key Takeaway
Capability is a real accident added to the body, proven by varying capacity without bodily change.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The First Capability: Precedes the Act and Suits Opposites
Nasafi states the consensus that the first capability precedes the act and gives examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the nature of the first capability, its precedence over the act, and its neutrality to opposites.

Core Idea
The first capability is soundness of limbs; it precedes the act and is neutral.

Imam Nasafi begins by establishing a point of agreement: all who affirm human capability agree that the first capability comes before the act. He illustrates this with clear examples and notes a key property: this capability is neutral, equally usable for obedience or sin.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the first capability
Read the Arabic passage once, noting that it discusses the first capability. Then read the translation to understand the examples.
The first capability is defined by examples.
2
Examine the examples of precedence
Notice that a healthy hand precedes seizing, a healthy leg precedes walking, and provisions precede pilgrimage. These show that the first capability exists before the act.
This establishes temporal precedence.
3
Reflect on suitability for opposites
The passage states that the same hand is suitable for both jihad and fighting Muslims, and the same leg for both walking to mosque and to sinful places. This shows the first capability is neutral and not specific to one act.
This neutrality will contrast with the second capability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أجمع القائلون بالاستطاعة المثبتون للعبد الأعمال أن الاستطاعة الأولى تتقدم الفعل، فإن اليد السليمة والرجل الصحيحة يتقدمان البطش والمشي، والزاد والراحلة يتقدمان وجود أفعال الحج، وكذلك يصلح للضدين، فإن اليد الصحيحة كما تصلح لجهاد الكفار تصلح لقتال أهل الإسلام، وكذا الرجل السليمة كما تصلح للمشي إلى المساجد تصلح للمشي إلى بيوت الخمارين والزواني. فأما الاستطاعة الثانية فقد اختلفوا في جواز تقدمها على الفعل، فزعمت المعتزلة والضرارية : أنها تكون سابقة على الفعل ويستحيل اقترانها به، وإليه ذهب أكثر الكرامية. وقال أصحابنا وجميع متكلمي أهل الحديث والنجارية: إنها تكون مع الفعل ومحال تقدمها على الفعل.
Then those who affirm capability and who affirm actions for the servant agreed that the first capability precedes the act. For the sound hand and the healthy leg precede seizing and walking, and provisions and the riding beast precede the performance of the actions of pilgrimage. Likewise, it is suitable for opposites, for the sound hand is suitable for jihad against the disbelievers as it is suitable for fighting the people of Islam, and likewise the healthy leg is suitable for walking to the mosques as it is suitable for walking to the houses of wine-sellers and fornicators. As for the second capability, they differed regarding the permissibility of its preceding the act. The Mu‘tazila and the Dirariyya claimed that it precedes the act and that its being concurrent with it is impossible, and most of the Karamiyya inclined to that. Our companions (the Maturidis) and all the theologians of the Ahl al-Hadith and the Najjariyya said: it is concurrent with the act and its preceding the act is impossible.
Source pages p. 131

Commentary
This passage is a classification and doctrinal report on the two types of capability. It first states the unanimous agreement among those who affirm a real capability for the servant that 'the first capability' (al-istiṭā‘a al-ūlā) precedes the act. This first capability is identified with soundness of limbs and means (e.g., a healthy hand precedes striking, provisions precede pilgrimage). It is also suitable for opposites: the same hand that can fight disbelievers can fight Muslims, and the same leg that goes to the mosque can go to sinful places. This indicates it is neutral and not specific to one act. Then the passage turns to 'the second capability' (al-istiṭā‘a al-thāniya), which is the accident of capability itself. On this, there is disagreement. The Mu‘tazila and Dirariyya hold that it precedes the act and cannot be simultaneous with it. Most of the Karamiyya also follow this view. In contrast, the author's school (the Maturidis) together with all the theologians of Ahl al-Hadith and the Najjariyya hold that the second capability is concurrent with the act and that it is impossible for it to precede the act. This is because, as implied elsewhere, the accident cannot endure, so if it preceded the act it would cease to exist at the moment of action, leaving the act without capability.

Key Terms
استطاعة أولى
تقدم
ضدان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Human capability only exists at the moment of action.
Correction: The first capability, such as a healthy hand, exists before the act and makes action possible.

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Nasafi mention that the hand is suitable for both jihad and fighting Muslims?
A) To show that the first capability precedes the act
B) To show that the first capability is neutral to opposites
C) To show that the first capability is identical to the second
D) To show that the first capability is not from Allah

Key Takeaway
The first capability (soundness of limbs and means) always precedes the act and is neutral, usable for good or evil.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your hand and foot are sound and equally capable of acts of worship or sin. Which direction have you turned them today? How will you ensure they are used for what pleases Allah before the capability is taken away?
?
The same leg that carried you to the mosque could carry you to a place of disobedience. What is your intention behind each step? Have you considered that every movement of your limbs is a trust from Allah and will be accounted for?
?
You have been given provisions and health to perform Hajj, but you could also use them for worldly pursuits. What does your use of these blessings reveal about your priorities? What concrete change will you make starting today to align your actions with your faith?

The Second Capability: Disagreement on Its Timing
Nasafi reports the disagreement on the second capability showing two opposing positions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the disagreement among Islamic theological schools regarding whether the second capability precedes or is simultaneous with the act.

Core Idea
The Mu‘tazila say the second capability precedes; the Maturidis say it is concurrent.

After establishing the first capability, Imam Nasafi turns to the second — the actual accident of capability. Unlike the first, there is no consensus. He reports the positions of the Mu‘tazila, Dirariyya, Karamiyya, and then the Maturidis and Ahl al-Hadith. This distinction is crucial for understanding divine power and human responsibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the second capability
Read the Arabic passage focusing on 'al-istiṭā‘a al-thāniya'. The translation will clarify the two opposing views.
The second capability is a separate concept from the first.
2
Note the groups and their positions
Identify which groups say the second capability precedes the act (Mu‘tazila, Dirariyya, most Karamiyya) and which say it is concurrent (Maturidis, Ahl al-Hadith, Najjariyya).
This is a clear sectarian divide.
3
Consider the theological implications
Think about why this disagreement matters: if capability precedes, then the act is separate from the ability; if concurrent, then ability and act happen together, affecting questions of free will and divine power.
The Maturidi view ties capability directly to the act to avoid implying a gap.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم أجمع القائلون بالاستطاعة المثبتون للعبد الأعمال أن الاستطاعة الأولى تتقدم الفعل، فإن اليد السليمة والرجل الصحيحة يتقدمان البطش والمشي، والزاد والراحلة يتقدمان وجود أفعال الحج، وكذلك يصلح للضدين، فإن اليد الصحيحة كما تصلح لجهاد الكفار تصلح لقتال أهل الإسلام، وكذا الرجل السليمة كما تصلح للمشي إلى المساجد تصلح للمشي إلى بيوت الخمارين والزواني. فأما الاستطاعة الثانية فقد اختلفوا في جواز تقدمها على الفعل، فزعمت المعتزلة والضرارية : أنها تكون سابقة على الفعل ويستحيل اقترانها به، وإليه ذهب أكثر الكرامية. وقال أصحابنا وجميع متكلمي أهل الحديث والنجارية: إنها تكون مع الفعل ومحال تقدمها على الفعل.

For the sound hand and the healthy leg precede seizing and walking, and provisions and the riding beast precede the performance of the actions of pilgrimage. Likewise, it is suitable for opposites, for the sound hand is suitable for jihad against the disbelievers as it is suitable for fighting the people of Islam, and likewise the healthy leg is suitable for walking to the mosques as it is suitable for walking to the houses of wine-sellers and fornicators. This first capability is identified with soundness of limbs and means (e.g., a healthy hand precedes striking, provisions precede pilgrimage). اقتران
تقدم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Both the first and second capabilities precede the act.
Correction: According to Ahl al-Sunna, the first precedes, but the second is concurrent.

Checkpoint
According to the Maturidis, what is the relationship of the second capability (al-istiṭā‘a al-thāniya) to the act?
A) It precedes the act.
B) It is concurrent with the act.
C) It follows the act.
D) It is identical to the first capability.

Key Takeaway
The second capability (the accident of power) is concurrent with the act according to the Maturidis, while the Mu‘tazila hold it precedes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider your own actions today. Do you tend to think you have the ability to act before you do it, or do you realize that the ability is given to you precisely at the moment of action? How does this lesson's distinction between the two positions make you more aware of your complete dependence on Allah for even your smallest acts? Will you pause before your next action to acknowledge that your power is not your own but a gift from Him?
?
The Mu'tazila assert that capability precedes the act to preserve human responsibility. Does your heart lean toward that view because it feels fair? Or can you accept the Maturidi view that capability is concurrent, which removes any claim of prior power and deepens your need for divine grace? How will this realization change the way you seek Allah's help before you speak or act today?

The Disagreement on Whether Capacity Is Suitable for Opposites
The author presents the disagreement on whether capacity is suitable for opposites, including views of Abu Hanifa, Ash'aris, and al-Maturidi's inclination.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the different positions on whether capacity (istita'ah) is suitable for opposites, including the views of Abu Hanifa, the Ash'aris, and al-Maturidi's inclination.

Core Idea
The suitability of capacity for opposites is a key point of disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Ash'aris.

The question of whether human capacity can be used for both obedience and disobedience (opposites) has deep implications for divine justice and human responsibility. In this passage, the author classifies the major positions: those who say capacity is suitable for opposites, those who limit it by substitution, and those who deny any suitability. Let's explore the reasoning behind each view.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three main groups
The passage first mentions those who hold capacity precedes the act (suitable for opposites), then those who hold it is concurrent with the act: Abu Hanifa's group (substitution), and the Ash'aris (not suitable). Notice also al-Maturidi's position.
The groups are defined by whether capacity is before or with the act.
2
Focus on Abu Hanifa's view of substitution (badal)
Abu Hanifa held that capacity is suitable for opposites by way of substitution: a single capacity can be for either, but not both simultaneously. Contrast this with the Ash'ari view that capacity is specific to its object.
The term 'badal' is key: it means substitution, not simultaneity.
3
Note al-Maturidi's stance
Al-Maturidi presented the disagreement without refutation, but his speech indicates he inclines toward the view that capacity is not suitable for opposites. Observe how he treats the Mu'tazila on both paths.
4
Reflect on the broader significance
Consider how this debate connects to free will and predestination. If capacity is not suitable for opposites, then each act requires a specific capacity from Allah, emphasizing divine control. If suitable by substitution, human choice plays a larger role.
This discussion touches on the core of the Qadr debate.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واختلفوا في كونها صالحة للضدين فقال جميع من زعم أن الاستطاعة قبل الفعل : إنها تصلح للضدين كما تصلح لذلك الأسباب والآلات. واختلف القائلون بأنها مع الفعل في ذلك فقال أبو حنيفة: إنها تصلح للضدين على طريق البدل، ومعنى ذلك أن الاستطاعة التي حصل بها الإيمان صلحت له ولا تصلح للكفر إذا اقترنت بالإيمان، ولكنها لو كانت اقترنت بالكفر بدلاً من اقترانها بالإيمان لصلحت له بدلاً من صلاحها للإيمان، وتابعه على هذا القول ابن الراوندي وأبو العباس القلانسي من متكلمي أهل الحديث وأبو العباس ابن سريج من فقهاء أصحاب الحديث. وقالت الأشعرية وجميع متكلمي أهل الحديث سوى القلانسي وابن سريج: إن القدرة لا تصلح للضدين، وإن قدرة الإيمان لا تصلح للكفر وهي غير قدرة الكفر وكذا على القلب، وكذا هذا من قدرة الطاعة وقدرة المعصية وهو قول الحسين بن محمد النجار. والشيخ الإمام أبو منصور الماتريدي ذكر الخلاف وذكر الحجج لكل فريق ولم يشتغل بالجواب لحجج أحد الفريقين، ولم يظهر أنه إلى أي قول يميل، وتكلم عن المعتزلة على الطريقين جميعًا، وأكثر كلامه يدل أنه يميل إلى أنها لا تصلح للضدين.
They disagreed on whether it (capacity) is suitable for opposites. All who claimed that capacity is before the act said: it is suitable for opposites just as causes and instruments are suitable for that. And those who said that it is with the act disagreed on that. Abu Hanifa said: it is suitable for opposites by way of substitution, and the meaning of that is that the capacity by which faith occurs is suitable for faith and is not suitable for disbelief when it is conjoined with faith, but if it had been conjoined with disbelief instead of its conjunction with faith, it would have been suitable for it instead of its suitability for faith. He was followed in this opinion by Ibn al-Rawandi, Abu al-Abbas al-Qalanisi among the mutakallimun of ahl al-hadith, and Abu al-Abbas Ibn Surayj among the jurists of the companions of hadith. The Ash'aris and all mutakallimun of ahl al-hadith except al-Qalanisi and Ibn Surayj said: capacity is not suitable for opposites, and the capacity for faith is not suitable for disbelief and it is other than the capacity for disbelief, and likewise the reverse, and likewise this applies to the capacity for obedience and the capacity for disobedience. And this is the opinion of al-Husayn ibn Muhammad al-Najjar. And the Shaykh Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi mentioned the disagreement and mentioned the proofs for each group, and he did not occupy himself with answering the proofs of either group, and it does not appear to which opinion he inclines, and he spoke about the Mu'tazila on both paths, but most of his speech indicates that he inclines to the view that it is not suitable for opposites.
Source pages p. 132

Commentary
This passage classifies opinions on whether capacity (istita'ah) is suitable for opposites (salih li al-diddain). The author first notes that all who hold that capacity precedes the act agree it is suitable for opposites, like other means and instruments. Then he turns to those who hold capacity is concurrent with the act. Among them, Abu Hanifa held it is suitable for opposites by way of substitution (badal): the capacity used for faith is suitable for faith and not for disbelief when conjoined with faith, but if it had been conjoined with disbelief it would have been suitable for disbelief. He was followed by Ibn al-Rawandi, al-Qalanisi, and Ibn Surayj. In contrast, the Ash'aris and most mutakallimun of ahl al-hadith except these two hold that capacity is not suitable for opposites: the capacity for faith is distinct from the capacity for disbelief. This is also the view of al-Husayn ibn Muhammad al-Najjar. Finally, al-Maturidi's stance is reported: he mentioned the disagreement without refuting either side, but his discourse indicates he leans toward the view that capacity is not suitable for opposites.

Key Terms
استطاعة
ضدين
بدل
قدرة
صالحة للضدين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think Abu Hanifa's view means a single capacity can produce both opposites simultaneously.
Correction: Abu Hanifa explicitly says it is by way of substitution (badal): the capacity is suitable for only one at a time, not both together.

Checkpoint

B) Abu Hanifa

Key Takeaway
The debate over whether capacity is suitable for opposites reveals fundamental differences in how Muslim theologians understood the relationship between divine omnipotence and human agency.

?
Abu Hanifa believed that the same capacity could have served either faith or disbelief, but Allah's decree determined which one. Does this give you comfort or cause you to reflect on your own choices? How does your trust in Allah's decree shape your daily struggle?

Refuting the Objection on Change in Substance
Nasafi refutes the objection about change in substance by analyzing attribution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Imam al-Nasafi refutes the objection that change in a substance does not require a new attribute if the substance was never devoid of that description.

Core Idea
Attribution is never from the essence itself; it always requires a distinct meaning.

In kalam, change in a substance (e.g., from rest to motion) is explained by the acquisition of new meanings. But what if the substance was never devoid of a certain description? Does change then still require a new meaning? An opponent raises this objection, and Imam al-Nasafi offers a clear logical refutation based on the nature of attribution (ittiṣāf). This lesson unpacks his argument.

Guided Path
1
Understand the objection
Read the opponent's argument: if a substance can never be devoid of a description, change does not require a new meaning because the description is always present.
Notice the conditional: if it is possible for the substance to be devoid, then change requires a meaning; if impossible, then not.
2
Analyze the refutation
Nasafi first dismisses the objection as ignorant, then gives a key principle: attribution is either from the essence or from a meaning. If the essence exists but attribution is impossible, then attribution must be from a meaning.
He uses the impossibility of being devoid (even for a moment) to prove that attribution is not from the essence.
3
See the absurd consequence
If attribution were from the essence, then we would have the absurd situation where the cause (essence) exists but the effect (attribution) is impossible. Nasafi illustrates this with the example of blackness.
This reductio ad absurdum shows that the only rational position is that change requires a real meaning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسأل بعضهم: إن تغير الجوهر عما كان عليه إنما يوجب التغير بوجود معنى زائد على الذات إذا جاز وجود الجوهر متعريًا عن ذلك الوصف أوقاتًا، فأما إذا لم يجز تعريه عنه ولا وقتا واحدًا ووجب تغيره في الثاني من حال حدوثه لا محالة لم يجب به حدوث معنى فيه. قلنا هذا كلام من لا يدري ما يقول، وهذا لأن الاتصاف إما أن يكون لأجل الذات، وإما أن يكون لمعنى، وإذا وجد الذات واستحال الاتصاف علم أن الاتصاف ليس من موجبات الذات، فعلم أنه من موجبات المعنى لأن الذات لو وجد وانعدم جواز الاتصاف كان الاتصاف من موجبات المعنى دون الذات، فإذا مع كان الاتصاف مستحيلاً مع وجود الذات كان أولى أن يكون الاتصاف موجب معنى وراء الذات لا موجب الذات. يحققه أن الاتصاف لو كان من موجبات الذات وقد وجدت الذات واستحال الاتصاف لكان فيه القول باستحالة ثبوت الحكم وإن تحققت العلة وهذا ظاهر الفساد ولو جاز هذا لجاز أن يقوم السواد بذات ويستحيل اتصافه بأنه أسود ثم في الزمان الثاني يجب اتصافه به وهذا محال لم يقل به أحد من العقلاء.
And one of them asked: The change of the substance from what it was only necessitates change by the existence of a meaning additional to the essence if it is possible for the substance to exist devoid of that description at times. But if it is not possible for it to be devoid of it even for one moment, and its change in the second [moment] from the state of its occurrence is necessary without fail, then it is not necessary that change of meaning occurs in it. We said: This is the speech of one who does not know what he says. This is because attribution (al-ittiṣāf) is either on account of the essence (al-dhāt) or on account of a meaning (maʿnā). When the essence exists and attribution is impossible, it is known that attribution is not from the necessaries (mūjibāt) of the essence, so it is known that it is from the necessaries of the meaning because if the essence existed and the possibility of attribution were non-existent, then attribution would be from the necessaries of the meaning not the essence. Thus, since attribution is impossible with the existence of the essence, it is more fitting that attribution is a necessitator of a meaning beyond the essence, not a necessitator of the essence. He verifies: If attribution were from the necessaries of the essence and the essence existed and attribution were impossible, then it would entail saying that establishment of the judgment is impossible even if the cause is realized, and this is obviously corrupt. And if this were permissible, then it would be permissible for blackness to subsist in an essence and for its attribution as black to be impossible, then in the second moment its attribution with it becomes necessary. And this is absurd; no rational person has said it.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage presents an objection and the author's response. The opponent argues: If a substance changes from one state to another, this change requires a new meaning only if the substance was sometimes devoid of that description. But if it was never devoid (e.g., it is always either moving or at rest), then change does not require a new meaning; it is just a change of the substance itself. The author refutes this by analyzing the nature of attribution (ittiṣāf). He states that attribution is either due to the essence itself or due to a meaning. If the essence exists and attribution is impossible, that proves attribution is not from the essence, so it must be from a meaning. He then gives a logical verification: If attribution were from the essence, then when the essence exists and attribution is impossible, that would entail that the judgment (the attribution) cannot be established even if its cause (the essence) is present, which is absurd. He gives an example: blackness subsisting in an essence but the essence not being described as black, then later it becomes black—this is nonsensical. The only rational position is that change requires a real meaning.

Key Terms
اتصاف
ذات
معنى
موجبات
جوهر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If a substance is never devoid of a description, then change of that description does not require a new attribute.
Correction: Imam al-Nasafi shows that impossibility of being devoid actually proves that the description comes from a meaning, not the essence, so change does require a new attribute.

Checkpoint
According to the author, what is the key factor in determining whether change requires a new meaning?
A) Whether the substance changes at all.
B) Whether it is possible for the substance to be devoid of the description at some time.
C) Whether the essence itself changes.
D) Whether the description is necessary or contingent.

Key Takeaway
Change in a substance always requires a real attribute (meaning) because attribution is never a necessity of the essence itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider the changes in your own character—like becoming more generous over time—do you treat those changes as mere fluctuations of your essence, or do you acknowledge that real new qualities (meanings) have been acquired? How does this lesson call you to reexamine your understanding of personal growth?
?
The objector assumed that if a description is always present, it must be from the essence itself. Are there areas in your faith where you mistakenly treat God's attributes as identical to His essence, avoiding the distinction that the scholars made? How willing are you to accept the logical necessity of real attributes, even if it challenges your comfort?
?
Nasafi called the objector's speech 'the speech of one who does not know what he says.' Do you have any assumptions about change or causality that you have not examined logically? What would it take for you to submit to rational proofs even when they contradict your initial intuitions?

Why Change Requires a Real Attribute: The Core Argument
Verification and dialectical question on change requiring a real attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why an essence that does not necessitate a description initially cannot later acquire that description without a real change in the essence.

Core Idea
No description arises from an essence without a real cause.

Imām al-Nasafī now deepens the argument that change requires a real attribute. He presents a verification and a dialectical question to show that if a description were merely from the essence, it would always be present or never change. This lesson unpacks that core reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Read the verification passage
Read the Arabic passage from 'yuḥaqqiquhū' to 'hādhā muḥāl'. Notice how the author sets up a conditional: if the essence does not cause the description initially, it cannot cause it later without change.
The argument assumes no change in essence.
2
Identify the absurd consequences
The author gives examples: incapacity cannot become power, ignorance cannot become knowledge without a cause. These illustrate why the opponent's view is absurd.
These examples are meant to be impossible.
3
Understand the dialectical question
Read the next part about descriptions that can be absent. The author asks opponents why they consider such descriptions as real attributes. The answer shows the inconsistency in their reasoning.
This question targets those who accept that some descriptions can be absent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحققه أن الذات لو لم توجب وجود الاتصاف في الأول ثم في الثاني عين ذلك الذات الذي لم يوجب الاتصاف واستحال وجود الاتصاف معه أوجب الاتصاف من غير تغيير ولا حدوث معنى فيه لوجب أن يقال: إن العجز وإن وجد في أول أحوال وجوده واستحال اتصاف الذات الذي قام به العجز بكونه قادرًا يوجب في الثاني كونه قادرا، وكذا الذات الذي قام به الجهل يوجب كون الذات في الثاني عالمًا وإن استحال اتصافه في أول الأحوال، وهذا محال. ثم يقال لهم: الوصف الذي كان يجوز كون الجوهر متعريًا عند أوقاتا لم كان وصف المعنى؟ ألأجل أنه إذا انعدم مع وجود الذات علم أنه ليس من موجبات الذات أم لأجل معنى آخر؟ فإن قال بالثاني، كلف إبرازه ولا قدره له عليه، وإن قال بالأول فقد أقر بما يوجب بطلان سؤاله هذا، وظهر أن لا فرق بين جواز التعري وقتا واحدًا وبين جوازه أوقاتا كثيرة. ثم يقال: لو كان بغير الوصف مع جواز بقائه متعريا عنه يوجب حدوث معنى كان بغيره مع استحالة بقائه متعريًا عنه أولى، ولولا حدوث المعنى الذي اضطر إلى تغير وصفه لجاز وجوده على ما كان عليه قبله. ثم يقال لهم: إذا استحال كون الجوهر متحركاً أو ساكنا في حال الحدوث واستحال بقاؤه عليه متعريًا عنهما بعد لم يحتج إلى حدوث معنى من أجله صار متحركًا أو ساكنا، فإذا كان هذا مستحيلاً ولم يكن جائزا عند أهل التوحيد ولم يكن بد من القول بوجود الحركة أو السكون دل ذلك على بعض ما قلتموه. فإن قيل: هذا الاستدلال مبني على مقدمة مجحودة وهي: أنكم ادعيتم استحالة الوصف بالبقاء
He verifies: If the essence did not necessitate the existence of attribution in the first [moment], then in the second [moment] it is the same essence that did not necessitate attribution and attribution with it was impossible, yet it necessitates attribution without any change or occurrence of meaning in it, then it would be necessary to say: Incapacity (al-ʿajz) though it existed in the first states of its existence and attribution of the essence in which incapacity subsists as being powerful was impossible, yet in the second moment it necessitates its being powerful; likewise, the essence in which ignorance (al-jahl) subsists necessitates the essence in the second moment as knowing (ʿālim) even though its attribution [with knowledge] was impossible in the first states. And this is absurd. Then it is said to them: The description which it was possible for the substance to be devoid of at times — why was it a description of meaning? Is it because when it is absent with the existence of the essence it is known that it is not from the necessaries of the essence, or is it for another meaning? If they say the second, they are required to produce it and they have no power to do so. And if they say the first, then they have conceded what necessitates the invalidity of this question of theirs, and it becomes clear that there is no difference between the possibility of being devoid for one time and its possibility for many times. Then it is said: If with the possibility of its remaining devoid of the description, [the change] necessitates the occurrence of a meaning, then with the impossibility of its remaining devoid of it, it is more fitting [to necessitate a meaning]. And were it not for the occurrence of the meaning which forced the change of its description, its existence would be permissible as it was before. Then it is said to them: When it is impossible for the substance to be moving (mutaharrikan) or at rest (sākinan) in the state of origination, and it is impossible for it to remain after that devoid of both, then it does not need the occurrence of a meaning due to which it became moving or at rest? But if this is impossible and not permissible according to the people of tawḥīd, and there is no alternative but to affirm the existence of motion or rest, then that indicates some of what you have said. And if it is said: This reasoning is built on a disputed premise, namely: that you have claimed the impossibility of description with persistence (al-baqāʾ)...
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage contains a series of further arguments. First, a verification: if the essence does not necessitate attribution initially, it cannot later necessitate it without change or a new meaning. Otherwise, absurd consequences follow: a substance with incapacity would become powerful without change, etc. Then a dialectical question: why do you (opponents) consider a description which the substance can be devoid of at times to be a description of meaning? Is it because absence with existence of essence proves it is not from the essence? If so, then you have conceded that the same logic applies even if it is devoid for only one moment. Then another argument: if possibility of being devoid necessitates a meaning, then impossibility of being devoid is even more compelling. Finally, an argument about motion and rest: a substance in its origination cannot be both moving and at rest, and thereafter cannot remain devoid of both—so it must have either motion or rest, which are real attributes. The passage ends with a possible objection: the opponent might dispute the premise that the substance cannot be described with persistence originally. The text cuts off here.

Key Terms
ذات
اتصاف
عجز
جهل
قدرة
علم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that a description can arise from an essence spontaneously without a real attribute.
Correction: The passage shows that if an essence does not cause a description initially, it cannot cause it later without change; otherwise, contradictory attributes would arise.

Checkpoint
What absurd consequence does the author derive from the assumption that an essence can change its description without a real attribute?
A) Incapacity would become power without cause.
B) Substance would be both moving and at rest.
C) Time would be meaningless.
D) Opponents would be silent.

Key Takeaway
Any change in description of an essence requires a real cause; otherwise, contradictory attributes would arise.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you experience a positive change in your character—like gaining patience or humility—do you attribute it to a real cause (such as practice, dua, or divine grace) or do you assume it just happened? How does this lesson push you to acknowledge your dependence on external causes, especially Allah’s help?
?
This lesson shows that an essence cannot change without a real cause. In your own life, have you ever expected yourself to change (e.g., stop a sin, increase in worship) without actually putting in causes or seeking the means? What does this teach you about the necessity of actively seeking causes for spiritual change?
?
If you believe that Allah can change your heart without any cause from you, does that make you passive? How does the proof in this lesson (that change requires a real attribute) actually inspire you to take responsibility for your own transformation, while still relying on Allah as the ultimate cause?

The Argument from Motion and Rest for Real Attributes
Further reasoning using motion and rest to prove real attributes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the impossibility of a substance remaining devoid of motion or rest proves the need for real attributes.

Core Idea
If a substance cannot be without a description, that description must come from a real cause.

Imām al-Nasafī now strengthens his argument with the example of motion and rest. A substance cannot originate as both moving and at rest, and it cannot later escape both descriptions. This forces the conclusion that such descriptions arise from real attributes.

Guided Path
1
Read the argument on the principle of impossibility
Read the first part: if mere possibility of being devoid necessitates a meaning, then impossibility of being devoid is even more compelling.
This is a logical a fortiori argument.
2
Focus on the motion/rest example
The author then applies this to motion and rest: a substance at origination cannot be both; after origination it cannot be devoid of both. It must have one or the other, and this requires a real attribute.
This example concretizes the abstract principle.
3
Consider the objection about persistence
The passage ends with a possible objection: opponents may deny that the substance cannot be described with persistence initially. This shows the debate continues.
The text cuts off here, but the objection is important.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يحققه أن الذات لو لم توجب وجود الاتصاف في الأول ثم في الثاني عين ذلك الذات الذي لم يوجب الاتصاف واستحال وجود الاتصاف معه أوجب الاتصاف من غير تغيير ولا حدوث معنى فيه لوجب أن يقال: إن العجز وإن وجد في أول أحوال وجوده واستحال اتصاف الذات الذي قام به العجز بكونه قادرًا يوجب في الثاني كونه قادرا، وكذا الذات الذي قام به الجهل يوجب كون الذات في الثاني عالمًا وإن استحال اتصافه في أول الأحوال، وهذا محال. ثم يقال لهم: الوصف الذي كان يجوز كون الجوهر متعريًا عند أوقاتا لم كان وصف المعنى؟ ألأجل أنه إذا انعدم مع وجود الذات علم أنه ليس من موجبات الذات أم لأجل معنى آخر؟ فإن قال بالثاني، كلف إبرازه ولا قدره له عليه، وإن قال بالأول فقد أقر بما يوجب بطلان سؤاله هذا، وظهر أن لا فرق بين جواز التعري وقتا واحدًا وبين جوازه أوقاتا كثيرة. ثم يقال: لو كان بغير الوصف مع جواز بقائه متعريا عنه يوجب حدوث معنى كان بغيره مع استحالة بقائه متعريًا عنه أولى، ولولا حدوث المعنى الذي اضطر إلى تغير وصفه لجاز وجوده على ما كان عليه قبله. ثم يقال لهم: إذا استحال كون الجوهر متحركاً أو ساكنا في حال الحدوث واستحال بقاؤه عليه متعريًا عنهما بعد لم يحتج إلى حدوث معنى من أجله صار متحركًا أو ساكنا، فإذا كان هذا مستحيلاً ولم يكن جائزا عند أهل التوحيد ولم يكن بد من القول بوجود الحركة أو السكون دل ذلك على بعض ما قلتموه. فإن قيل: هذا الاستدلال مبني على مقدمة مجحودة وهي: أنكم ادعيتم استحالة الوصف بالبقاء
He verifies: If the essence did not necessitate the existence of attribution in the first [moment], then in the second [moment] it is the same essence that did not necessitate attribution and attribution with it was impossible, yet it necessitates attribution without any change or occurrence of meaning in it, then it would be necessary to say: Incapacity (al-ʿajz) though it existed in the first states of its existence and attribution of the essence in which incapacity subsists as being powerful was impossible, yet in the second moment it necessitates its being powerful; likewise, the essence in which ignorance (al-jahl) subsists necessitates the essence in the second moment as knowing (ʿālim) even though its attribution [with knowledge] was impossible in the first states. And this is absurd. Then it is said to them: The description which it was possible for the substance to be devoid of at times — why was it a description of meaning? Is it because when it is absent with the existence of the essence it is known that it is not from the necessaries of the essence, or is it for another meaning? If they say the second, they are required to produce it and they have no power to do so. And if they say the first, then they have conceded what necessitates the invalidity of this question of theirs, and it becomes clear that there is no difference between the possibility of being devoid for one time and its possibility for many times. Then it is said: If with the possibility of its remaining devoid of the description, [the change] necessitates the occurrence of a meaning, then with the impossibility of its remaining devoid of it, it is more fitting [to necessitate a meaning]. And were it not for the occurrence of the meaning which forced the change of its description, its existence would be permissible as it was before. Then it is said to them: When it is impossible for the substance to be moving (mutaharrikan) or at rest (sākinan) in the state of origination, and it is impossible for it to remain after that devoid of both, then it does not need the occurrence of a meaning due to which it became moving or at rest? But if this is impossible and not permissible according to the people of tawḥīd, and there is no alternative but to affirm the existence of motion or rest, then that indicates some of what you have said. And if it is said: This reasoning is built on a disputed premise, namely: that you have claimed the impossibility of description with persistence (al-baqāʾ)...
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage contains a series of further arguments. First, a verification: if the essence does not necessitate attribution initially, it cannot later necessitate it without change or a new meaning. Otherwise, absurd consequences follow: a substance with incapacity would become powerful without change, etc. Then a dialectical question: why do you (opponents) consider a description which the substance can be devoid of at times to be a description of meaning? Is it because absence with existence of essence proves it is not from the essence? If so, then you have conceded that the same logic applies even if it is devoid for only one moment. Then another argument: if possibility of being devoid necessitates a meaning, then impossibility of being devoid is even more compelling. Finally, an argument about motion and rest: a substance in its origination cannot be both moving and at rest, and thereafter cannot remain devoid of both—so it must have either motion or rest, which are real attributes. The passage ends with a possible objection: the opponent might dispute the premise that the substance cannot be described with persistence originally. The text cuts off here.

Key Terms
حركة
سكون
جوهر
حدوث
بقاء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that motion and rest are just accidental states that do not require real attributes.
Correction: The argument shows that because a substance cannot be devoid of both motion and rest at any time after origination, these descriptions must be caused by real attributes.

Checkpoint
According to the argument about motion and rest, why must a substance have a real attribute of motion or rest?
A) Because it cannot be both moving and at rest at the same time.
B) Because it cannot remain devoid of both motion and rest after origination.
C) Because motion and rest are opposites.
D) Because the opponent admits this is necessary.

Key Takeaway
The necessity of a description like motion or rest at all times after origination proves it cannot be from the essence alone but requires a real attribute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Does your own experience of being 'at rest' or 'in motion' feel like it comes from your own essence, or do you recognize that these states are given to you by a real cause beyond yourself? If they were from your essence, you would never change—yet you do. What does this constant change in your very existence tell you about your need for the One who causes every description?
?
The passage argues that even a mere substance cannot be without a description. You are more than a substance—you have a soul, intellect, and choices. If even a simple entity requires a real attribute for its descriptions, how much more do you depend on a real Creator for every one of your qualities—your strength, your knowledge, your very life? Can you truly say you attribute every good in you to Him alone?
?
When you consider the description of persistence (بقاء) mentioned in the objection, think: Do you take for granted that you continue to exist? This lesson shows that even the fact that you remain the same from one moment to the next is not automatic—it requires a real cause. Have you ever thanked God for keeping you in existence, moment by moment, as a real act of His mercy?
